klogv1OutputCallDepth = 6\n\n// klogv1DefaultPrefixLength is the length of the log prefix that we have to strip out.\nconst klogv1DefaultPrefixLength = 53\n\n// klogv1Writer is used in It is inspired\n// by klog's upstream klogv1/v2 coexistence example:\n// https://github.com/kubernetes/klog/blob/main/examples/coexist_klog_v1_and_v2/coexist_klog_v1_and_v2.go\nfunc (klogv1Writer) Write(p []byte) (n int, err error) {\n\tif len(p) < klogv1DefaultPrefixLength {\n\t\tklogv2.InfoDepth(klogv1OutputCallDepth, string(p))\n\t\treturn len(p), nil\n\t}\n\n\tswitch p[0] {\n\tcase 'I':\n\t\tklogv2.InfoDepth(klogv1OutputCallDepth, string(p[klogv1DefaultPrefixLength:]))\n\tcase 'W':\n\t\tklogv2.WarningDepth(klogv1OutputCallDepth, string(p[klogv1DefaultPrefixLength:]))\n\tcase 'E':\n\t\tklogv2.ErrorDepth(klogv1OutputCallDepth, string(p[klogv1DefaultPrefixLength:]))\n\tcase 'F':\n\t\tklogv2.FatalDepth(klogv1OutputCallDepth, string(p[klogv1DefaultPrefixLength:]))\n\tdefault:\n\t\tklogv2.InfoDepth(klogv1OutputCallDepth, string(p[klogv1DefaultPrefixLength:]))\n\t}\n\n\treturn len(p), nil\n}\n\nvar (\n\tappName = 94→\n    95→type watchAddRemover interface {\n    96→\tAdd(path string) error\n    97→\tRemove(path string) error\n    98→}\n    99→type noopWatcher struct{}\n   100→\n   101→func (noopWatcher) is canceled.\n   105→// eventHandler() must be non-nil, and pollInterval must be greater than 0.\n   106→// eventHandler() is invoked whenever a change event is observed or pollInterval elapses.\n   107→// errorHandler() is invoked (if non-nil) whenever an error occurs initializing or watching the specified path.\n   108→//\n   109→// If path is a directory, only the directory and immediate children are watched.\n   110→//\n   111→// If path does not exist or cannot be watched, an error is passed to errorHandler() and eventHandler() is called at pollInterval.\n   112→//\n   113→// 116→// in case the path changed concurrent with calling WatchUntil().\n   117→func WatchUntil(ctx context.Context, pollInterval time.Duration, path string, eventHandler func(), errorHandler func(err 171→\t\t\t}\n   172→\n   173→\t\t\t// Try to re-establish the watcher if we previously got a watch error\n   174→\t\t\tif attemptPeriodicRewatch {\n   175→\t\t\t\t_ = watcher.Remove(path)\n   176→\t\t\t\tif err := watcher.Add(path); err != nil {\n   177→\t\t\t\t\terrorHandler(err)\n   178→\t\t\t\t} else {\n   179→\t\t\t\t\tattemptPeriodicRewatch = false\n   180→\t\t\t\t}\n   181→\t\t\t}\n 189→\t\t\t\treturn\n   190→\t\t\t}\n   191→\n   192→\t\t\t// Try to re-establish the watcher for events which dropped the existing watch\n   193→\t\t\tif e.Name == path && (e.Has(fsnotify.Remove) || interface {\n\t// Initializes the watcher with the given watch handlers.\n\t// Called before all other methods.\n\tInit(FSEventHandler, FSErrorHandler) error\n\n\t// Starts listening for events and errors.\n\t// When an event or error occurs, the corresponding handler is called.\n\tRun()\n\n\t// Add a filesystem path to watch\n\tAddWatch(path string) error\n}\n\n// FSEventHandler is called when a fsnotify event occurs.\ntype FSEventHandler func(event fsnotify.Event)\n\n// FSErrorHandler is called when a fsnotify error occurs.\ntype FSErrorHandler func(err error)\n\ntype fsnotifyWatcher struct {\n\twatcher      *fsnotify.Watcher\n\teventHandler FSEventHandler\n\terrorHandler FSErrorHandler\n}\n\nvar _ FSWatcher = &fsnotifyWatcher{}\n\n// NewFsnotifyWatcher returns an implementation of FSWatcher that continuously listens for\n// fsnotify events and calls the event handler as soon as an event is received.\nfunc NewFsnotifyWatcher() FSWatcher {\n\treturn &fsnotifyWatcher{}\n}\n\nfunc (w *fsnotifyWatcher) AddWatch(path string) error {\n\treturn w.watcher.Add(path)\n}\n\nfunc (w *fsnotifyWatcher) Init(eventHandler FSEventHandler, errorHandler FSErrorHandler) error {\n\tvar err error\n\tw.watcher, err = fsnotify.NewWatcher()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\tw.eventHandler = eventHandler\n\tw.errorHandler = errorHandler\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (w *fsnotifyWatcher) Run() {\n\tgo func() {\n\t\tdefer w.watcher.Close()\n\t\tfor {\n\t\t\tselect {\n\t\t\tcase event := <-w.watcher.Events:\n\t\t\t\tif w.eventHandler != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\tw.eventHandler(event)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tcase err := <-w.watcher.Errors:\n\t\t\t\tif w.errorHandler != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\tw.errorHandler(err)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}()\n}\n\ntype watchAddRemover interface {\n\tAdd(path string) error\n\tRemove(path string) error\n}\ntype noopWatcher struct{}\n\nfunc (noopWatcher) Add(path string) error    { return nil }\nfunc (noopWatcher) Remove(path string) error { return nil }\n\n// WatchUntil watches the specified path for changes and blocks until ctx is canceled.\n// eventHandler() must be non-nil, and pollInterval must be greater than 0.\n// eventHandler() is invoked whenever a change event is observed or pollInterval elapses.\n// errorHandler() is invoked (if non-nil) whenever an error occurs initializing or watching the specified path.\n//\n// If path is a directory, only the directory and immediate children are watched.\n//\n// If path does not exist or cannot be watched, an error is passed to errorHandler() and eventHandler() is called at pollInterval.\n//\n// Multiple observed events may collapse to a single invocation of eventHandler().\n//\n// eventHandler() is invoked immediately after successful initialization of the filesystem watch,\n// in case the path changed concurrent with calling WatchUntil().\nfunc WatchUntil(ctx context.Context, pollInterval time.Duration, path string, eventHandler func(), errorHandler func(err error)) {\n\tif pollInterval <= 0 {\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Errorf(\"pollInterval must be > 0\"))\n\t}\n\tif eventHandler == nil {\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Errorf(\"eventHandler must be non-nil\"))\n\t}\n\tif errorHandler == nil {\n\t\terrorHandler = func(err error) {}\n\t}\n\n\t// Initialize watcher, fall back to no-op\n\tvar (\n\t\teventsCh chan fsnotify.Event\n\t\terrorCh  chan error\n\t\twatcher  watchAddRemover\n\t)\n\tif w, err := fsnotify.NewWatcher(); err != nil {\n\t\terrorHandler(fmt.Errorf(\"error creating file watcher, falling back to poll at interval %s: %w\", pollInterval, err))\n\t\twatcher = noopWatcher{}\n\t} else {\n\t\twatcher = w\n\t\teventsCh = w.Events\n\t\terrorCh = w.Errors\n\t\tdefer func() {\n\t\t\t_ = w.Close()\n\t\t}()\n\t}\n\n\t// Initialize background poll\n\tt := time.NewTicker(pollInterval)\n\tdefer t.Stop()\n\n\tattemptPeriodicRewatch := false\n\n\t// Start watching the path\n\tif err := watcher.Add(path); err != nil {\n\t\terrorHandler(err)\n\t\tattemptPeriodicRewatch = true\n\t} else {\n\t\t// Invoke handle() at least once after successfully registering the listener,\n\t\t// in case the file changed concurrent with calling WatchUntil.\n\t\teventHandler()\n\t}\n\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n\t\t\treturn\n\n\t\tcase <-t.C:\n\t\t\t// Prioritize exiting if context is canceled\n\t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Try to re-establish the watcher if we previously got a watch error\n\t\t\tif attemptPeriodicRewatch {\n\t\t\t\t_ = watcher.Remove(path)\n\t\t\t\tif err := watcher.Add(path); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\terrorHandler(err)\n\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\tattemptPeriodicRewatch = false\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Handle\n\t\t\teventHandler()\n\n\t\tcase e := <-eventsCh:\n\t\t\t// Prioritize exiting if context is canceled\n\t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Try to re-establish the watcher for events which dropped the existing watch\n\t\t\tif e.Name == path && (e.Has(fsnotify.Remove) || e.Has(fsnotify.Rename)) {\n\t\t\t\t_ = watcher.Remove(path)\n\t\t\t\tif err := watcher.Add(path); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\terrorHandler(err)\n\t\t\t\t\tattemptPeriodicRewatch = true\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Handle\n\t\t\teventHandler()\n\n\t\tcase err := <-errorCh:\n\t\t\t// Prioritize exiting if context is canceled\n\t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// If the error occurs in response to calling watcher.Add, re-adding here could hot-loop.\n\t\t\t// The periodic poll will attempt to re-establish the watch.\n\t\t\terrorHandler(err)\n\t\t\tattemptPeriodicRewatch = true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n","numLines":217,"startLine":1,"totalLines":217}}}

Implementation\\n\\n**1. File Watcher Setup**\\n\\n`pkg/util/filesystem/watcher.go` provides the core file watching abstraction via the `WatchUntil()` function, which uses fsnotify for efficient file system event monitoring with fallback to periodic polling. The `FSWatcher` interface abstracts file watching with callbacks for events and errors.\\n\\n`cmd/kube-proxy/app/options.go` demonstrates practical usage: `initWatcher()` creates and initializes an fsnotify watcher, `eventHandler()` processes write/rename events, and `runLoop()` orchestrates the proxy server lifecycle with the watcher running in a goroutine.\\n\\n`pkg/kubelet/config/file_linux.go` implements similar patterns for kubelet: `doWatch()` creates an fsnotify watcher for pod manifest files, and `produceWatchEvent()` translates fsnotify events (Create, Write, Chmod, Remove, Rename) into pod add/modify/delete events without process restart.\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection**\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` uses byte-level comparison (`bytes.Equal()`) to detect configuration changes and `reflect.DeepEqual()` for semantic equality checking. The `checkFile()` function reads the config file, compares bytes with the cached `lastReadData`, and only proceeds with reload if data differs.\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authenticator/config.go` implements per-component config diffing through health checks before atomic swap—the `updateAuthenticationConfig()` function validates new JWT authenticators with `healthCheck()` before committing the change.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (No Connection Drop)**\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` with `Store()` for lock-free atomic swap. The pattern:\\n1. Construct new authorizer in `newForConfig()`\\n2. Atomically swap via `current.Store()` \\n3. Reads use `r.current.Load().authorizer.Authorize()` - new requests immediately see the new config without blocking\\n4. The swap is instantaneous, never dropping in-flight requests\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authenticator/config.go` similarly uses `atomic.Pointer[jwtAuthenticatorWithCancel]` with `Swap()`, which atomically exchanges the old and new authenticators. Importantly, it schedules async cleanup of the old authenticator after a grace period (1 minute + 30 second sleep) to allow in-flight requests to complete using cached metrics.\\n\\n### Prometheus Implementation\\n\\n**1. File Watcher Setup**\\n\\n`config/reload.go` contains the `GenerateChecksum()` function that computes SHA256 hashes of the main config file plus all referenced rule files and scrape config files. This enables change detection without continuous fsnotify watching.\\n\\n`cmd/prometheus/main.go` implements the reload mechanism with three triggers:\\n- SIGHUP signal via `signal.Notify(hup, syscall.SIGHUP)`\\n- Web API endpoint via `webHandler.Reload()` channel\\n- Periodic polling via `time.Tick()` at configurable `autoReloadInterval`\\n\\nThe polling loop (lines 1289-1335) continuously monitors for config file changes by comparing checksums, enabling hot-reload without explicit file watching infrastructure.\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection**\\n\\nPrometheus uses SHA256-based checksums computed over:\\n- The main YAML configuration file content\\n- All glob-expanded rule file paths and contents\\n- All glob-expanded scrape config file paths and contents\\n\\nThe `GenerateChecksum()` function (config/reload.go) hashes:\\n1. Main config file content\\n2. For each rule file: path prefix + content\\n3. For each scrape config file: path prefix + content\\n\\nThis detects not only config changes but also changes in included files. Comparison at line 1321 (`currentChecksum == checksum`) determines if reload is necessary.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (No Connection Drop)**\\n\\nPrometheus uses a \\\"reloader\\\" pattern where `reloadConfig()` (lines 1600-1645):\\n1. Loads new config via `config.LoadFile()`\\n2. Iterates through registered reloaders (scrape.Manager, notifier.Manager, discovery.Manager, storage.remote.Storage, web.Handler, tsdb.DB, etc.)\\n3. Calls `ApplyConfig()` on each reloader - these are implemented with:\\n   - `sync.Mutex` guards (`mtx.Lock()/Unlock()`) for thread-safe updates\\n   - Reloaders update internal state atomically within the lock:\\n     - `scrape/manager.go` ApplyConfig updates scrape pools without stopping existing scrapers\\n     - `notifier/manager.go` ApplyConfig reuses existing alertmanager connections (via config hash mapping)\\n     - `discovery/manager.go` ApplyConfig keeps running providers as-is when configs haven't changed\\n     - `storage/remote/storage.go` ApplyConfig updates read and write clients in-place\\n     - `web/web.go` ApplyConfig simply updates the config pointer within the lock\\n     - `tsdb/db.go` ApplyConfig updates retention policies without blocking queries\\n\\n4. Updates metrics (`configSuccess`, `configSuccessTime`) to reflect reload status\\n5. Invokes callback for notification system\\n\\nThe entire reload is sequential but fast, and because ApplyConfig implementations use fine-grained locking only around state update moments, long-running requests continue uninterrupted. New requests immediately see the new configuration after the ApplyConfig phase completes.\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\nKubernetes uses **event-driven file watching** (fsnotify) with per-component atomic pointers for config swaps, while Prometheus uses **periodic checksum polling** with a centralized reloader pattern that calls ApplyConfig on multiple components. Both approaches achieve the same goal: configuration hot-reload without process restart or dropped connections, but through different architectural patterns suited to their respective use cases.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":40,"cache_creation_input_tokens":334,"cache_read_input_tokens":80993,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":334},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7a05f7c5-6b95-4a82-bac9-869ebc4524e0","uuid":"6b47e18b-a1e0-41e2-82cc-53d325d83db4"}

The `FSWatcher` interface abstracts file watching with callbacks for events and errors.\\n\\n`cmd/kube-proxy/app/options.go` demonstrates practical usage: `initWatcher()` creates and initializes an fsnotify watcher, `eventHandler()` processes write/rename events, and `runLoop()` orchestrates the proxy server lifecycle with the watcher running in a goroutine.\\n\\n`pkg/kubelet/config/file_linux.go` implements similar patterns for kubelet: `doWatch()` creates an fsnotify watcher for pod manifest files, and `produceWatchEvent()` translates fsnotify events (Create, Write, Chmod, Remove, Rename) into pod add/modify/delete events without process restart.\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection**\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` uses byte-level comparison (`bytes.Equal()`) to detect configuration changes and `reflect.DeepEqual()` for semantic equality checking. The `checkFile()` function reads the config file, compares bytes with the cached `lastReadData`, and only proceeds with reload if data differs.\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authenticator/config.go` implements per-component config diffing through health checks before atomic swap—the `updateAuthenticationConfig()` function validates new JWT authenticators with `healthCheck()` before committing the change.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (No Connection Drop)**\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` with `Store()` for lock-free atomic swap. The pattern:\\n1. Construct new authorizer in `newForConfig()`\\n2. Atomically swap via `current.Store()` \\n3. Reads use `r.current.Load().authorizer.Authorize()` - new requests immediately see the new config without blocking\\n4. The swap is instantaneous, never dropping in-flight requests\\n\\n`pkg/kubeapiserver/authenticator/config.go` similarly uses `atomic.Pointer[jwtAuthenticatorWithCancel]` with `Swap()`, which atomically exchanges the old and new authenticators. Importantly, it schedules async cleanup of the old authenticator after a grace period (1 minute + 30 second sleep) to allow in-flight requests to complete using cached metrics.\\n\\n### Prometheus Implementation\\n\\n**1. File Watcher Setup**\\n\\n`config/reload.go` contains the `GenerateChecksum()` function that computes SHA256 hashes of the main config file plus all referenced rule files and scrape config files. This enables change detection without continuous fsnotify watching.\\n\\n`cmd/prometheus/main.go` implements the reload mechanism with three triggers:\\n- SIGHUP signal via `signal.Notify(hup, syscall.SIGHUP)`\\n- Web API endpoint via `webHandler.Reload()` channel\\n- Periodic polling via `time.Tick()` at configurable `autoReloadInterval`\\n\\nThe polling loop (lines 1289-1335) continuously monitors for config file changes by comparing checksums, enabling hot-reload without explicit file watching infrastructure.\\n\\n**2. Config Diff Detection**\\n\\nPrometheus uses SHA256-based checksums computed over:\\n- The main YAML configuration file content\\n- All glob-expanded rule file paths and contents\\n- All glob-expanded scrape config file paths and contents\\n\\nThe `GenerateChecksum()` function (config/reload.go) hashes:\\n1. Main config file content\\n2. For each rule file: path prefix + content\\n3. For each scrape config file: path prefix + content\\n\\nThis detects not only config changes but also changes in included files. Comparison at line 1321 (`currentChecksum == checksum`) determines if reload is necessary.\\n\\n**3. Atomic Config Swap (No Connection Drop)**\\n\\nPrometheus uses a \\\"reloader\\\" pattern where `reloadConfig()` (lines 1600-1645):\\n1. Loads new config via `config.LoadFile()`\\n2. Iterates through registered reloaders (scrape.Manager, notifier.Manager, discovery.Manager, storage.remote.Storage, web.Handler, tsdb.DB, etc.)\\n3. Calls `ApplyConfig()` on each reloader - these are implemented with:\\n   - `sync.Mutex` guards (`mtx.Lock()/Unlock()`) for thread-safe updates\\n   - Reloaders update internal state atomically within the lock:\\n     - `scrape/manager.go` ApplyConfig updates scrape pools without stopping existing scrapers\\n     - `notifier/manager.go` ApplyConfig reuses existing alertmanager connections (via config hash mapping)\\n     - `discovery/manager.go` ApplyConfig keeps running providers as-is when configs haven't changed\\n     - `storage/remote/storage.go` ApplyConfig updates read and write clients in-place\\n     - `web/web.go` ApplyConfig simply updates the config pointer within the lock\\n     - `tsdb/db.go` ApplyConfig updates retention policies without blocking queries\\n\\n4. Updates metrics (`configSuccess`, `configSuccessTime`) to reflect reload status\\n5. Invokes callback for notification system\\n\\nThe entire reload is sequential but fast, and because ApplyConfig implementations use fine-grained locking only around state update moments, long-running requests continue uninterrupted. New requests immediately see the new configuration after the ApplyConfig phase completes.\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\nKubernetes uses **event-driven file watching** (fsnotify) with per-component atomic pointers for config swaps, while Prometheus uses **periodic checksum polling** with a centralized reloader pattern that calls ApplyConfig on multiple components. Both approaches achieve the same goal: configuration hot-reload without process restart or dropped connections, but through different architectural patterns suited to their respective use cases.\"\n    56→}\n    57→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
